So it's impossible to bypass its USB firmware and check whether the hard disk itself was really dead. There was "Not For Resale" printed on its white label.

Right now, a short piece of cellulose tape was used to stick the fan blade to the axel, so that the fan blade could not wobble with loud noise!

16 May
  • Pry open the Asus RT-N18U using a steel ruler, along the front edge of the router. The circuit board has the printing "ASUS RT-N18U REV 2.20". The 3 capacitors (4E4-100-16V, E479-300-6.3V, 470-25A-K64) are clean, no leakage of fluid. Not sure whether they are solid capacitors. No bulging as well. I found no burnt marks on the dark cyan PCB, front and back. I haven't removed the big heatsink, which is unnecessary as the firmware was basically working fine. The 4-pin serial header J3 is now visible and accessible. There are two kind of induction coils labeled "1419 HN36201CG" for the LAN ports, and one coil labelled "1419 HN18101CG" for the WAN port. Would they affect connection?
  • The top plastic cover of Asus RT-N18U is so tightly sealing the router that I don't know why 4 screws are needed.
  • Because all LAN ports are dead, serial recovery using the J3 jumper is impossible as TFTP needs a LAN port. I don't think the serial port allow local uploading of file.
14 May
  • After flashing Asus RT-N18U with DD-WRT build 56359 and a cold-boot, the router's four LAN ports no longer responded. The firmware however was still responding to pressing of the RESET button.
26 Apr
  • The remote for the i-Mation DVR-6005 DMB-TH TV Set-top Box had a few buttons not working. After being un-used for months and without AAA bacteries, most buttons went back to normal except the Right Arrow Button. Today I did a factory reset, all buttons worked!

Then I remember that the Antec TPN-650 power supply had a damaged 24-pin connector. So I re-arranged and re-plugged all power-related cables from the power supply, which seemed to finally fix the problem.

  • Monitor got no signal out of the DVI connector out of the HP Radeon 7750 GPU. Turned out that hook-like pin 24 in the male plug of the VGA to DVI-A connector was bent. I was not alerted of the poor insertion felt when plugging in the connector. Also, the pin problem did NOT affect the DVI connection of the Radeon R9 285 GPU.

24 Dec
  • Installed the 5.25" Drive Bay Speaker into the Asrock J3455M PC. Needed to plug in the $23 headset to PC cable to enable headphone out of the front panel audio header. Now the PC became an AM radio tuned to RTHK Station 5 over internet.

  • The 12V 40mm exhaust fan (Nidec D05X-12TL, Made in Vietnam) at the back of the Sony CMT-M333NT Micro Hi-Fi was dead as well. The Evercool 40mm fan (Made in Taiwan) from the old PowerLeap socket 370 adapter was a possible replacement. But their power cables needed to be swapped (2-pin vs 3-pin).
17 Dec
  • Bought a Sama 120mm LED Fan at HK$20 from Hang Chong of New Golden.
16 Dec
  • Spent roughly 4 hours upgrading the Window$ 8 Home in the HP Envy H9 Pheonix PC to Window$ 10 Home. The process began with running the Cyberlink Recovery Manager in the Micron 120G SSD to reinstall Win 8 cleanly without personal data (backup first if you got data). Because Win 8 was too old, you need to first enable TLS over HTTP using registry and KB3140245. Then you could run Windows Update like normal to upgrade Win 8 to its most recent build. This might need hours using a wired connection to internet. After that, you could download then run Win 10's Media Creation Tool, and upgrade the old Win 8 directly to Win 10, skipping Windows 8.1.
  • You might wanna skip Win 10 and directly go for Windows 11, but this would be your own trial.
  • Now that Win 10 was installed, one could use a new and bigger SATA SSD to install Win 10 directly from Win 10 ISO *without* the HP Win 8 Recovery Manager. That will use far less time than going through the 8-to-10 upgrade process. But the process converted the Win 8 OEM/VLS product key to Win 10 digital entitlement. It's just a "digital entitlement" because you didn't pay for a real Win 10 product key.
  • If TLS over HTTP was not enabled, Win 8 would report error 0x800072F8F during Windows Update. Then Win 10 Media Creation Tool would report error 0x80072EE7. The Internet Explorer in Win 8 could NOT access most websites because HTTPS is standard requirement now.
  • Four hours was really a waste of time. So I was doing other things while waiting for it. :)
  • Why didn't Micro$oft just provide a fast program just to convert eligeble Win 7/8/8.1 product key to Win 10 digital entitlement without the need to run Windows Update then Media Creation Tool for hours?
  • Using a new SSD to install Win 10 might break the Secured Boot feature in the UEFI BIOS of the HP Envy H9 PC. You can of course disable Secured Boot or rebuild it from the installed Win 10. I don't wanna try it now, not my non-business use.
  • BTW, I discarded the original black HP SATA cables in the H9 PC and replaced them with red cheap ones. That hopefully might prevent disk drive connection and detection issue reported by the original owner of this PC.
  • Speaking of Windows 11, Windows 12 might be released next year (2024), possibly with an A.I. theme! And Windows 10 will lose its Micro$oft support the following year (14th October 2025). I dunno whether Win 8 and Win 10 could be upgraded directly to Win 12 without payment in the future.
  • Windows 8 and 8.1 reached end of life on 10th January 2023; Internet Explorer 11, 30th November 2023.
01 Dec
  • There was a better trick to make the HP CH28N Blu-Ray Combo Drive eject its tray properly without replacing the motor belt. After the plastic tray was ejected, *slightly* twist the tray clockwise and anti-clockwise, just slightly. Do NOT use strong force.
11 Nov
  • Started using RAMdisk again with DDR4 RAM overclocked to 3500MHz. It was fast and stable. Maybe the Adata SX8200 Pro's SSD controller was not capable of working with very fast CPU memory controllers. Now that it was gone, everything running was OK. I just couldn't explain why it affected the BIOS.... could it be a protocol problem?
10 Nov
  • It really looked like all those overclocking problems in the past few years were caused by either directly by the faulty and possibly overheated Adata SX8200 Pro SSD, the use of both M.2 slots in the Gigabyte Z370-HD3P or just the hardened thermal paste on the Intel i7 CPU. The dust on the heatsink fins shouldn't be that a factor.
  • At this moment in time, there were ATX motherboards featuring DDR5-7600 RAM slots, PCIe 5.0 expansion slots, more than two Gen5 M.2 SSD and USB 4.x (Thunderbolt).
  • There were also very compact mini or dice PCs (dimension 12cm x 13cm x 6cm) that could play DirectX games. Big desktop PCs might soon become a niche market for hobbyists.
  • And we got USB Type-C virtual-reality headsets (built-in cameras for tracking eyes and devices) and palm sense controllers (six-axis motion sensing system: three-axis gyroscope, three-axis accelerometer) as well, as in Playstation VR2.
01 Nov
  • Overclocking the DDR4 RAMs with multiplier=35 at 1.32V (again NOT using XMP profiles)! No ramdisk, CPU FAN and SYS 2 FAN at full speed.
26 Oct
  • Using a cutter, peeled off the sticky heatsink metal strip off Adata SX8200 Pro along its longer edges, and removed the warranty label (Voltage 3.3V, S/N: 2I5020043866). Controller: Silicon Motion SM2262ENG BA, T29X73.24, TW 2D. Cache: 2 x Nanya 2GB DDR3 NT5CC12W16JR-2K. Memory: 4 x Micron 128GB 8UA2D NW926 (TLC).
25 Oct
  • Overclocking the DDR4 RAMs with multiplier=32 at 1.29V (again NOT using XMP profiles)! No ramdisk, CPU FAN and SYS 2 FAN at full speed.
24 Oct
  • Used water to clean the heatsink of CoolerMaster Hyper 212X CPU Cooler. Re-applied thermal paste (Gelid GC Extreme) over the CPU.
  • The Adata SX8200 Pro M.2 SSD is double-sided but with only 512G of storage space. The AGI Rapidity Pro is also double-sided, but has 2TB of storage.
22 Oct
  • Overclocking the 4 sticks of Crucial DDR4 RAMs with multiplier=30 at 1.29V (not using XMP profiles). CPU FAN, System FAN 1 and System FAN 2 were at full speed.
  • Trying to overclock the 4 sticks of DDR4 RAMs with multiplier=32 at 1.28V, but they were not stable enough. It was very likely a heat issue, as the thermal paste on the CPU should have dried up by now. And there were not that many heatsinks to cool the motherboard overall, unlike more expensive products. The problem worsened with fast M.2 SSDs installed, which generated more heat than SATA SSD, and directly onto the motherboard. Using RAM disks in Window$ might add more heat, too.
21 Oct
  • Suddenly, the Adata SX8200 Pro M.2 SSD was dead. I always thought that the problem was the AGI Rapidity Pro because it disappeared first when the PC hanged in UEFI mode. It looked like the BIOS failed to get past the detection of the Adata SX8200 Pro M.2 SSD after it stalled, which caused the disappearance of the other M.2 SSD (AGI Rapidity Pro).
  • Reinstalled Windows 10 Pro in the AGI Rapidity Pro. Needed to use DISKPART to clean the partition table and reboot first.
  • The death of the Adata SX8200 Pro made the BIOS behave strangly. It suddenly reported the Intel i7-9700KF having an internal GPU, which was wrong. I needed to use Restore Optimized Defaults in the BIOS to fix it.
  • Whenever Win 10 hanged, the disk activity LED was always lit. This might overheat the Adata SSD, causing it to self-destruct. I dunno why its SSD controller didn't throttle itself or better stop working.
  • Owning to the strange BIOS of Gigabyte Z370-HD3P, I was using CSM mode to boot the Win 10 Pro installed via UEFI mode and GPT partitions. In CSM mode, the M.2 SSDs were less likely to disappear.

  • Bought a 120mm ARGB Fan (color: white) at HK$38 from New Golden.
  • The fan's LED and motor were powered separately. Though my motherboard had only one 12V RGB header, I suspect I could connect the power and ground pins of the 5V ARGB plug to just turn on the LED without an expensive ARGB controller nor ARGB-to-RGB adapter. Not sure whether the default state of the ARGB LED was ON or OFF. :)

  • The Toshiba 3.5" 2TB SATA hard disk (DT01ACA200) bought on 12 Oct 2013 from Centralfield was dead. It looked like a click-of-death, with only one partition barely mountable. It was stored in a Maxtor 60GB foam box.

?? Jul
  • Since the A12025-20CB-4BP-F1 fan of CoolerMaster Hyper 212X was dead, I broke the fan into components using a slip-joint plier left by my father. The fan's blade was bolted along the axile of the fan, which meant you cannot repair nor clean it. You could not replace nor re-use the fan blade as well. The flat doughnut-like circuit board had a chip labelled "LB11961 3RR7", which was a Single-Phase Full-Wave Fan Motor Drive (made by ON Semiconductor formerly Sanyo) according to Google Search. There was quite a large 16V 22uF "CD110" capacitor.
  • There was what looked like black burnt mark on the circuit board right under the LB11961.

15 Jul
  • Installed Windows 11 into the Adata SX8200 Pro SSD after clearing all system partitions in all SATA hard disks and the ones in AGI SSD. But the Win 11 failed to boot in UEFI mode. Needed to clear CMOS and enabled CSM mode to boot the Win 11.
  • I found some Google results (notably a YouTube video) about setting the EFI partition to support booting via both UEFI and BIOS (non-UEFI) mode by executing command "bcdboot c:\window /s efi_drive: /s all".
  • With the BIOS in CSM (non-UEFI) mode, the BIOS will report errors about hardware settings and allows you to restore to defaults. This is unlike UEFI mode.
06 Jul
  • Today, room temperature (without air-conditioning) had risen to 32 Celsius with humidity 68%. The Core i7-9700KF kept freezing Windows 10 when DDR4 RAM modules were running at multipler 32 (also XMP profile). Fiddling with timing paramters didn't help. My only option was to remove all RAM overclcoking setttings, and set Multipler and DRAM Voltage to Auto (which were 24, 1.2V respectively). Is the memeory controller, and XMP profile, of i7-9700KF really that sensitive to hot weather? It's just a 2-degree rise from 30 Celsius in the past few days....
03 Jul
  • Uped the Turbo Boost Core Frequencies of Intel Core i7-9700KF to 49,48,47,46,45,41,41,41
  • Changed DDR4 Timing (CL-tRCD-tRP-tRAS): 15-17-17-35 with tRC=50
  • Now that I ejected the HP Blu-Ray Combo Optical Drive once daily, the door jam problem happened less frequently.
26 Jun
  • Now that it's summer with higher ambient temperature over 30 degree Celsius and without air-conditioning, the Gigabyte Z370-HD3P with Intel Core i7-9700KF CPU would freeze when using XMP profile of the DDR4 RAM with CPU settings at default. I suspect the memory controller on the CPU chip was overheated when XMP was enabled together with CPU Turbo Boost. Maybe the CoolerMaster Hyper 212X CPU Cooler was not efficient enough.
  • The solution to overclock the DDR4 RAM was to lower the max CPU Turbo Boost Frequency and inputting DDR4 voltage & timing parameters manually, without relying on any automatic XMP profiles.
  • The following were the BIOS parameters that overlocked the DDR4 RAMs without issues:
    • CPU Turbo Boost Core Frequencies: 46,43,42,41,41,40,40,40 (down from 49,48,48,47,47,46,46,46)
    • DDR4 parameters: voltage: 1.30V, Multiplier: 32, Timing (CL-tRCD-tRP-tRAS): 15-18-18-38 with tRC=56
    • Some suggested: tRAS=CL+tRCD, tRC=tRAS+tRP, tCAS=CL
    • Both CPU Fan and System Fan 1 were set to Full Speed.
  • When decreasing DDR4's CL from 16-18-18-38 to 15-18-18-38, you could notice that the browser loaded or refreshed web-pages faster.
10 Jun
  • Remember the mysterious disappeance of M.2 SSD during BIOS POST? It had nothing to do with the arrangement of DDR4 RAM moduloes, nor the CR2023 battery, nor the USB 2.0 ports, nor the need to clear CMOS. The solution is to drain all leftover electricty out of the PC before turning it back on again. Somehow leftover electricity kept old settings in some "memory", making the BIOS detect wrong status of various M.2 SSD drives. In general, the M.2 SSDs (especially the one containing Window$ 10) disappeared after Window$ crashed or froze, and when Window$ was using UEFI boot. Note that the EFI partition (for UEFI boot) was writtable at all time.
  • To drain all leftover electricity out of the PC, just unplug the power cord or switch off the power supply, then push the power button a few times. An interesting thing was that the LED of the DDR4 RAM would light up for a few seconds then extinguish after pushing the power button, but the PC didn't boot.
  • I didn't see anybody talking about this strangeness in various web forums about PC hardware... not with my Google Search keywords.
08 Jun
  • Bought Adata Gammix D20 DDR4-3600 2x8G at HK$374 from Comdex.
  • After just 2 years of button pushing, a few keys (A, S, O, Down-Arrow) of the Razer BlackWidow Lite TKL keyboard had lost its top plastic coating near their center.
02 Jun
  • Asrock J3455M booted successfully with both DDR3L RAM sticks installed. So the problem was likely the CR2032 battery. The battery issue, which led to clock error, might also have affected Windows Update KB5022352 for Windows Server 2012R2 Esseential.

2022

20 Nov
  • In the past 2 days, the AGI SSD kept disappearing after Windows 10 froze, possibly due to overheating. But then why did the SSD disappear from the UEFI boot even after the PC was turn off for a few minutes? The SSD should have been cool after that. Why did I need to clear BIOS to make the PC boot again?
  • Replaced the heatsink of AGI 2TB SSD to the one with copper, using 2 1mm thermo-pad. Also moved the AGI SSD to the M2A_32G slot near the CPU. Also attached the CoolerMaster Jetflo 120mm fan to the Hyper-X CPU cooler, and set the fan profile to a bit higher speed even at low load. That should increase air flow above the M2A_32G M.2 SSD slot, thus cooling the AGI 2TB double-sided SSD.
  • Rearranged the DDR4 RAMs again in this order: DDR4-3600, DDR4-3200 with damaged fingers, DDR4-3600, DDR4-3200. Locked the DRAM voltage to 1.33V, so that all DDR4 RAM could run at 3500Mhz (Multiplier=35).
  • Reduced the CPU Vcore to 1.28V while turning off "Enhanced Multi-core Performance (also known as Multi-Core Enhancement in other BIOSes). EMP/MCE will run all CPU cores simultanesouly. Now the i7-9700KF could work at factory settings (with Turbo Boost).

01 Aug
  • In the last few days, Win 10 in my Z370-HD3P PC kept freezing while I was merely surfing internet and listening to MP3. Whedn Win 10 froze, the BIOS could no longer detect the two M.2 SSDs (Adata and AGI) the following boot. The first solution was to unplug all DDR4 then plug in DDR4 RAM one-by-one. Clearing CMOS could also do. But Win 10 continued to freeze suddenly.
  • Today I re-arranged the DDR4 RAMs, DDR4 XMP profiles turned off, then maxed out the speed of both the side panel fan and CPU fan. I also moved the AGI OS SSD from M.2 slot M2Q_32G to slot M2A_32G near the CPU, and disabled Fast Boot. These steps seemed to solve the sudden freeze problem.
  • Nonetheless, overheating should not have made the BIOS to stop detecting the OS SSD at slot M2Q_32G. Also, boot problems caused by overheating should be gone after turning off the PC. It seemed that when in UEFI mode (CSM disabled), if Win 10 failed to shut down itself properly, the BIOS would ignore the UEFI boot manager in the corresponding OS drive. That's really weird.
  • The M2Q_32G is indeed hotter since it's next to the GPU PCIe x16 slot. This M.2 slot also supports SATA mode, and share the PCIe lane with the PCIe 4x slot.
  • Fan speed settings didn't change much the average temperature of the motherboard, which was about 45 degrees Celsius.
  • Another strange phenomena: sometimes when turning off some lamps, USB(?) connection sound was heard from my Win 10 PC.

  • Opened up the Akasa AK-ICR-14 USB 3.0 Internal Card Reader. It's actually a USB external card reader with a USB 3.0 port, with 2 USB cables fused into a USB 3.0 20-pin header plug. The card reader had just a circuit-board. Both USB 3.0 ports did feature 4 pins and 5 metal contacts, at least they looked like a regular USB 3.0 port. I think the circuit board could be packaged as a external card reader by just wrapping it with a plastic casing.
  • Looking up the specification of the Realtek RTS5301 chip via Google, I failed to find any direct reference to it, including Realtek's own website!! Some websites mixed it up with "RTS 5111", which looked more like a "USB 2.0 All-in-One Card Reader Controller"! There was mention of other chips like "RTS5304", "RTS5306" and "RTS5300". The paint of the label (both logo & text) on the chip didn't look like forged. Hopefully, it's not a spy eavedropping chip. Well... well... well...
  • Connected the Sony HCD CMT-M333NT Micro Hi-Fi Component System to the Windows$ Server PC using a USB printer cable. The CMT-M333 showed up as a "USB Audio Device" with "USB Audio CODEC" in Device Manager and no driver was needed. The WinServer PC could use it as an additional pair of speaker by setting CMT-M333's source to "PC". There was a driver to make CMT-M333 work as a NetMD from the PC, but that would require an old piece of software called SonicStage. Then you could use CMT-M333 to record audio from the PC. Without the custom 64-bit driver (official driver was 32-bit only), that funciton showed up as "SONY USB COMM" with hardware ID "USB\VID_054C&PID_008E".

21 Apr
  • After a night of ticking, the Concord watch's LCD panel blurred again, nearly invisible. Disassembled it, placed a piece of paper between the LCD panel and the circuit board (to force better connection between the LCD panel and the conductive rubber strip), and put things back. This time, the see-saw connector strip was properly installed. The LCD digits were a lot more black. The toggle switches could set date and time.
  • For twice the 1mm anode metal strip bounced away from the fine forcep. Luckily, it was found on the floor.
  • A website suggested using alcohol to clean the contact areas between the conductive rubber strip, the circuit board's terminals for the strip and the terminals on the glass LCD panel.
  • The proper name for conductive rubber strip is "Elastomeric connector", also known ZEBRA connector. "pitch" is used to describe the width of separation.
20 Apr
  • Disaseembled the Concord watch. Removed the see-saw connector strip from both sides of the watch, and then put things back together. Successfully made the conductve rubber strip to have better contact with the LCD panel. But this repair disabled the toggle switches used to set date and time.
  • Under the light from the 3M desktop lamp. the back of the Concord was grey. The reason: the filter of the the 3M desktop lamp is a polarizing filter. So is the watch's LCD panel.
  • At 23:59, the LR41 battery was inserted back into the watch. The watch started ticking at 12:00.

Extracted the motherboard and all disk devices out of the chassis, cleaned the dust inside of the computer chassis, then reassembled everything and re-arranged all cables. It seemed that the real problem was a loose 8-pin CPU power plug. In the process, a metal screw for mounting motherboard was lost. It's 3 hours of work.
  • In the trouble-shooting process, discovered that there are 2 switches for TPU and EPU in the Asus M5A99X EVO. Turned them all off. And it seemed that the very old Antec SP-400 400W could no longer be powered on after being idle for a long time. And 2 wires on the 3-pin fan cable repaired yesterday was broken again after testing it today.
  • Started using the Fujimax 16G Micro-SD card in Nokia 3170 fold. No disk errors after copying music MP3 into it.
24 Apr
  • Forgot to remove the 1.5V AA battery from the Konstar MT-1015B multimeter, which had not been used for years. The leads of the battery compartment was completely covered in cyan copper sulphate. The cathode of the 1.5V Duracell battery fractured. Even the metal at the tips of the fuse had some copper sulphate.
  • Checked that the two 1.5V AAA batteries inside the Uni-T UT33A multimeter are still in good shape.
  • Re-soldered the 3 loosen wires to the male end of the 3-pin fan extension cable, added heat-shrink tubing to protect the soldering.

16 Apr
  • The Asus M5A99X EVO froze when loading Win 10. After that, the motherboard could not complete the POST sequence. Opened the computer chassis and found that the POST sequence stopped at CPU test, with the red CPU LED lit continuously. I detached the Deepcool CPU heatsink and replaced the AMD FX-6800 with the Athlon II 245 and cleared the CMOS. All PCI and PCIe adapters were removed as well. The POST still stopped at CPU test as indicated by the red CPU LED.
  • By accident, after turning off then on the power supply twice in quick succession, the motherboard could finish POST sequence. I inserted the FX-6300 back into the motherboard and assembled the computer.
  • Not sure whether the POST problem was caused by weather change, the age of the M5A99X EVO motherboard, or the Antec power supply!

  • The Seagate 500G hard disk hadn't completely failed, It's still possible to copy data out of it, especially those files that had not been touched recently.
  • Installed the Hitachi HDS721050CLA362 500G hard disk into the Asrock J3455M PC. Configured it to use GPT partition and ReFS file system.
  • In retrospect, the Seagate 500G hard disk did demonstrate some signs of failure. The PC containing it sometimes could not be shutdown within 20 seconds. There was some delay in booting up as well.
  • CrystalDiskInfo, which read SMART data, marked the Seagate 500G hard disk as "Bad". The Uncorrectable Sector Count was 83; Current Pending Sector Count0, 80; Reallocated Sectors Count, 1 (raw value: 1AF0). Reallocated Sectors Count was colored red, while the previous 2 counts was colored yellow. Power up hours 0x4389 ~ 4.75 years.

I needed to manually set fan speed to maximum in order to prevent it freezing or crashing my Window 10. Could it be the thermal compound being dried up? Looking back, the GPU was in service for 3 years.
  • I noticed that the Radeon Crimson Relive driver did NOT always remember my manual fan settings. Bug? Feature? Well.... this could be a trick to "persuade" you to buy a new GPU!
  • At maximum fan speed setting, the R9 285 still registered a temperature of 60 degrees Celsius. I had only BOINC+SETI@Home running. I really think the default fan profile was over-optimistic. And it's not logical to play with fan speed settings via software. It's very much like dark magic.

  • Dell U2515H delivered. Manufactured Date printed Sep 2015.
  • Tested Dell U2515H's mini-DP and two HDMI ports. Monitor came with only a mini-DP to DP, and it worked. The monitor stand was spring-loaded, so that the monitor had to be mounted to adjust its height. No light bleeding or yellow tints were noticed. No dead or bright pixel were found.
  • The monitor's white was really bright, needed to reduce brightness:contrast from 50:50 to 25:25. However, the color would be too dim when wathcing movies. The white was definitely not as tainted as the Philips 220WS8FB.
  • At about 2 feet from the monitor, I needed to move my head to look at the edges of the monitor. Maybe it's a good for my eyes and neck.
  • The native resolution of Dell 2515H is 2560x1440. Needed up-scaled the text 150% for my old eyes to see it clearly. The bigger desktop definitely allowed more windows displayed.
  • Dell U2515H uses a touch-sensitive control panel. There is also a Dell Display Manager to change its settings from Window$. The Display Manager also offered a way to arrange opened windows.

  • Some suggested the following additional steps to prevent Windows 10 from being installed: taskkill /f /im GWX.exe
    taskkill /f /im GWXUX.exe
    cd/d C:\Windows\System32
    takeown /f GWX
    cacls GWX /e /g everyone:f
    rd/q/s GWX

    • Back panel: CoolerMaster 12cm fan from Hyper 212X blowing out
    • Side panel: CoolerMaster 12cm fan blowing out
    • DeepCool CPU heatsink using two 92mm fans blowing top-ward
    • A sheet of card-paper at the upper fan of the DeepCool heatsink stopping air from reaching the front panel

  • The SanDisk Extreme II SSD scored 748 in AS SSD Mark. Notice that this SSD uses the Marvell controller, which does not compress data. The SandForce controller, used by Adata SX900, does compress data to lengthen the life of the SSD.

22 Jul
  • Seemed that ImgBurn was tested against Micro$soft's AHCI driver only. When used with AMD's own amdsbs.sys/ahcix64s.sys driver, I needed to enable "Don't Use Immediate Disk I/O" to avoid errors.
21 Jul
  • With the deployment of the 128G SSD, the 2x1TB RAID 0 array was broken back into single disks and switched the SATA mode from RAID to AHCI. Now I could look at their SMART information. AMD's RAID mode did not provide SMART information, ulike Intel's RAID mode.
  • Something to do with UEFI boot: setting the first boot device of M5A99X EVO to the SSD would cause a boot problem. Needed to set the DVD drive (without a disc) as the first boot device.
  • Crystal DiskInfo (Shizuku Edition) flagged one of the 1TB hard disk as caution. Its "Reallocated Sectors Count" was 6. The other 1TB hard disk got 0.
  • In AHCI mode using Micro$oft's AHCI driver, AS SSD Benchmark score of the SSD reached 523. The sequential read speed reached 446.9 MBps. The read access time was 0.173 ms, still some 10 times slower than Intel solution. Something to do with SandForce's data compression?

  • AS SSD Benchmark scored only 261, with the read access time being 2 times slower than statistics out there. The Sequential Read Speed was just about 300MBps, rather than 450 MBps in SX900's specification. Read access time was 0.201 ms.

11 Aug 
Pythagorean: sqrt(162+92) = 18.36
Ratio of w:h:diag is thus: 16:9:18.36

So if the diagonal is 19":
width = (16/18.36)x19 = 16.6"
height = (9/18.36)x19 = 9.3"
area = 16.6*9.3 = 154 in2

A 4:3 19" monitor has 173 in2 of screen area, so you are losing about 13% 
desktop real estate. Better step up to a 21" or 24" if you want widescreen. 
 :-)

             | | | |
